Fast cart dim sum service. Seems to do alot of local regular business vs tourist. Huge stage and balcony for second floor seating. Was probably really fancy at one point. Pretty dated now. <user_name>Li Li</user_name><Date>1547054411842< /Date><rate>3< /rate><Text>Love the dim sum on carts, arriving steamy hot, tasted just as expected. Very crowded at times, with servers talking loudly to each other. Chaotic and disorganized environment. Tables and chairs were set tightly, So, you have to be super careful in trying to sit down without bumping the chair behind you. If you need an attention to order more drink or pay your bill , you must spend sometime looking around or wave or grab anyone attention because they seem to be on some kind of missions, excluding customer satisfaction. We were not sure who was our waiter. The bathrooms too need serious attention concerning cleanliness. Overall, it was ok experience. My preference is for somewhat calmer and organized establishments, with more attentive servers. So, if you wish for a relaxing good time eating dim sum, this is not the place for you. However, if you do not mind the noise and below average service, then, enjoy.<//Text>< Pics>

< text>
Don't expect anything fancy in this large venue, nor the deferential welcoming you may expect from any above-average restaurant. The staff can be a bit curt while accommodating you, and the servers may not be particularly fluent in English. However, service is swift and efficient, and for dim sum all you need is to point at what you'd like to try (or you can still easily order a la carte). The place is especially suitable for medium size groups and for families. And very reasonably priced.<//text>

<user_name>Catherine Desley<//user_name><Text>It's an interesting and delicious experience.  9/10 would go again
Be warned the meat plates are not necessarily hot due to being carted around, but certainly cooked.
Basically you flag down a cart, point at a plate, and it's added to your tab.  If you want more than one of the same plate, and you don't speak much Chinese, just hold up your fingers to indicate how many you want.  It's not the best place to spend too much time at the table, but it was more than worth the experience.  If you just want one or two plates or something it's cheaper elsewhere.  Best to bring friends as it's more worth the amount of food and experience you get,</Text><Pics>None</Pics>< userid>

<review>[from July 2006]

I was just at New Asia for a friend's wedding and -- though I was very happy to share this special day -- I wish I had been equally happy with the food.  Instead, it was bland and utterly uninspiring.  The McD's of dim sum.

The faded/peeling wallpaper and the soiled napkin originally placed at my table didn't exactly set a charming ambience, either.

Service was decent, sound system was fine.

But -- and true, this isn't the restaurant's fault -- whatever you do, DON'T PARK AT THE LOT HALF A BLOCK DOWN!  In big print, I saw "$2 per 30 minutes."  Okay, not cheap, but not bad.  Imagine my surprise and disgust, then, when I was told "$25".  Then I noticed the fine print ("$25 from 4 hours, 1 minute and onwards.")  I was parked for 4 hours and 7 minutes.  Bastards.<//review></record>

<user_name>Jessica Gong</user_name><Resp>None< /Resp><Pics>None<//Pics>< date>
1364350955928<//date>
< Text>
Did someone say Dim Sum?! Let's meet at New Asia!

I've been told that this place is a bit touristy but I disagree. What sets it apart from most other chinese restaurants that you may find in the area, is that it is HUGE and still fairly clean! It was designed for banquet sized events such as weddings.

This place has TWO levels. When they have tons of people they open up the second floor for customers to sit at and eat.

The food is absolutely delicious! The size of each item is oversized! You know you are getting your money's worth when you come here.

The little old chinese ladies are super friendly when they come by on their carts asking what you want to eat. If you speak canto, they are pretty fun to talk with while they are grabbing a steamer of food for you and stamping your card.

The only unfortunate part of this huge place, is the second floor. If you get there too late and get the boot the second floor, you are in a world of loneliness. They have to turn on the kitchen on the second floor, and re-organize the staff to accommodate both floors. So sometimes, the second floor gets ignored a bit. They won't necessarily pre-make all the stuff already prepared for the first floor. So you'll have to flag someone down to get what you want if you can't find it on the carts.< /Text>

<Text>Sundowner Inn or as it is now called, Days Inn by Wyndham, is a centrally located Inn right off Hwy 237 in Sunnyvale. Due to it's prime lication, commuters have quick access (by car) to all of Silicon Valley. The rooms are spacious and spotless, and have been recently renovated. I found my stay very comfortable. There are also wheelchair accessible rooms with great care taken to ensure full amenities and easy accessibility features (room 107 is a great example). Mr. Shah, the owner, continues to help his staff regularly, with the vigor and vim of a person a quarter of his age , even sometimes working the front desk on weekends, where he loves to meet his guests and give them an overview of the grounds, of which he takes great pride. There is a lovely pool on-site and breakfast is served daily at the pool cabana. There is also a Greek restaurant with tasty choices for everyone. My week-long stay was excellent, and I would highly recommend it if visiting the Sunnyvale, San Jose, or surroundings.< /Text>< pics>

115588798835511682572< /UserId.>
<name>Nathan McKinley Henderson< /name><Time>1416602921798<//Time>< Rate>
1< /Rate>
< review>
I ended up spending the nights of Monday - Thursday at the Days Inn in Sunnyvale.  It was the only thing that was close, still available, and under the hotel cap for my company, so I went for it.  I didn't realize it was a motel (strike 1), I didn't realize it was itty-bitty (strike 2), or that it didn't have wifi (strike 3), so I wasn't terribly happy on first arrival.  That night, I was made less happy by being woken up twice by loud rodent sounds coming from roughly under my bed.  Gross, but fine, I thought, I'll just make sure I eat all my meals out, not leave food anywhere, and not spend much time here until tomorrow night, when I can get my money back.

Except they wouldn't let me leave.  They told me first that I couldn't get a refund for the first night, which I thought was lousy but reasonable.  I had paid them for a night in a room, I guess I didn't specify it needed to be rat-free.  Then they told me that I couldn't get my money back for that night, or any of the other nights I was staying there.  "You can leave any time you like, but you can never check out," I guess.  I was pretty resigned at this point, so I asked if they could at least get me some traps I can set so I can sleep.  They said, and I quote this because it is so memorable, "We had the guy buy extra traps this week, but it looks like we're out."  Every part of that sentence is just wrong.  You cannot run a motel under these circumstances.  But no, resigned Nathan just asks if they can direct me to a hardware store so I can buy my own traps.  I figure I'll expense them!  I get the name of one down the street and she prints out Google Maps directions for me.  I follow the Google Maps directions, arrive at the hardware store: it's closed.

So I gave up and coped with it.  The second night I was there I finally got a glimpse of one of these. It was about the size of a soda can and was running from behind my nightstand to behind my bed.  Ugh.</review>

<Rate>4</Rate>< review>
This seems like a good deal for the price compared to other Santa Clara hotels and motels. The check-in experience could have been better, I think the 'new guy' checked me in.  Another guy reminded him to speak politely.  The room was nice and seems clean.  The furniture and flooring were in good shape.

Most of the pillows were too big and fluffy for me. Not as much as I have seen at other places though.  It's a good reminder to bring your own.

I did not test the wi-fi, check out the pool or try the coffee.

The towels were as you find most anywhere - white, scratchy and too small.

Parking seems adequate.

I would return here.

Update: I forgot to mention that to charge your phone on the nightstand you need to pull the furniture away from the wall to get to a plug.  The top plug was so loose my charger prongs wouldn't stay in the socket!< /review>

< Review>
I'm sitting in the room right now, debating if I can make it through the night hiding on top of this bed or if I need to go find another room or even sleep in the car. This is by far the worst hotel I've ever been in.
The front desk lady must have been depressed. Checked my friend into my room and me into his and told us to just not cause any issues in the rooms.
In the room, the lights all have sensors on the switches so the lights keep randomly turning on and off. There are cobwebs in the corners, black stains on the walls and the floor boards in the bathroom have all been torn out (probably due to the water damage under the sink).
The sheets and blankets look clean, but of course I'm too freaked out to look at the mattress under them. So I'm going to sleep on top of the blanket and use the blanket from the other bed next to me to keep me warm (this is again assuming I don't hear bugs crawling and abandon everything and sleep in the car).
So much for Days Inn having any semblance of a reliable brand. Avoid this place like it's the plague.<//Review>

<text>Afters is super amazing. I love how they can get the donut to be as hot as it is while still having the ice cream be really really cold inside. I always think that I'll be breaking my teeth while eating these milky buns but it turns out okay each time.

My favorite flavor is hands down, the cookie butter. Very similar to my overall favorite flavor, salted caramel, the cookie butter is sweet and savory. It goes really well with the milky bun which is also sweet. Their cookie monster flavor is also really good.

I've never been disappointed with this place. I think the milky buns are a much better version of what everyone's trying to do with ice cream fusions, like with cookies. They have so many flavors and they're patient with you trying the ones you find hitting your curiosity.

The staff is always quite friendly making Afters on the higher end of ice cream parlors out there. I always recommend this place to all my friends and you should definitely check it out.<//text><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipO-V_DEwNq2Hv6wnq0febHqsDixSWZIzCfy4nWd=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipObCP_kLKA8L9pK-ocKy3rg886tjG8s9_N9SR3S=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipO6V8fhSn8ihGmw02gCIXOsgVh4F8_j8aRyxvj9=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNPaTDm_3Nxm-YuxyuGjPxCIx_kAlSXeMonQPHI=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNouLs8_w3rgVl_iIvUgku1-qMvJot38qGJ2DdJ=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMjmOWWZFiX1lD-TgKWGX2vqUi_BNWpBsxOwzn6=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMN-Dpfjn0pjc6F9FKeqM1FcTBgT4RkzKGkP4iE=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOkTMW-0fcrNcFeWZnKUIWXSuQqjkBDVZcty7cx=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipP_cFntQH3vbOCT9AYROMuzt-D544LI8yLMX9mO=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPc70KaSFbbiQzmOgTpJOr7xauXtXWgbV7x9Zb9=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPn68uofTLZMLplCcPJvwXlGhQXQjAjIZUF3tIU=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNr5FfhwCxhoI4ms3kWkEseerjm_-ghmjKRNboN=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOBORHPxZex3d10ieImLMJcDCiiSIwcf23lWGM8=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMbgsWc0t_fuuTr--G63HTjlM8Iqq5Fq8u1kVE7=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNbffgz0-YtKISHHFzVfwTvyr7clBuwmp1_vEBv=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//Pics><name>Eleanor Ramsey<//name>< UserId.>

< Review>
The location is easy to miss since the signage is minimal, but trust me, you don't want to miss it. There are some really interesting ice cream concoctions like the blue cookie monster flavor with cookie pieces in it (their most popular flavor) or the peanut butter s'mores flavor, which I tried. I had my ice cream in a glazed milky bun, which tasted essentially like having my ice cream in a warm glazed doughnut. The soft, warm, sweet bun surrounded cold, creamy ice cream with crunchy pretzel pieces in it. SO GOOD! The store is pretty plain and doesn't have much ambiance, but if you're looking for a unique treat, this is the place to go.<//Review>

I've stood in line at night (since a friend insisted) and I've been able to waltz in with a few minutes wait in the daytime. I will say their ice cream is definitely, really delicious.

But ONLY their ice cream.

Their Milky Bun is the diabetes inducing treat that gets everyone all crazy but A) it's too sweet B) it's too sweet and C) even the non-glazed donut is too sweet.

It looks adorable though. They mash some ice cream in between 2 flat donuts and  then heat seal it so it's like a hot pocket. But. TOO SWEET.

I love just getting their ice cream in a WAFFLE cone. They make it really fresh here and it's ultra crispy!

Almond Cookie and Monster Mint Chip are what I crave.

Yum yum yum.<//Review>

<Rate>3<//Rate>< Review>
Tried the very hyped up "milky bun-" a glazed donut with ice cream. Although it is a unique dessert, overall for me it was too much sugar overload.

I went on a Sunday afternoon and the wait was about 25 minutes to get to try the ice cream. The decor is hip, sarcastic, and overall just very hipster.

They have a variety of interesting flavors and mixes: for the milky bun you get to choose a topping and they mix it with the ice cream and put it in a warm donut. The best ice cream I tried was jasmine tea- very refreshing and delicious. I instead got cookie butter with captain crunch because I thought the textures would go well.

$5 for this dessert is a little much for me, I'd rather have a cookie ice cream sandwich for half the price. Because of the price and wait, I think the Milky Bun isn't really worth it.< /Review>

<rating>5< /rating><GmapID>0x80dd27390c3fe7ab:0x98c5e2648edf90f4<//GmapID>< review>
I found out about this place on Instagram! A friend of mine made me drool on my phone after she waited hours in line for a milky bun and posted pictures.

Lucky for me I was traveling back to Cali anyway and had to add this on my list to try!  A local in town said to come early to beat the crowd, yes sir.

The biz sign is on the window made difficult to find unless you have really good eyes ha it just says ice cream in small letters on building, but let me save you the trouble it's sandwiched between a Chinese restaurant chain(forgot name!) and Hallmark in the left corner of the plaza.

They have a list of original ice cream names you won't find anywhere that I can think of,  had trouble deciding, wanted to try them all, ended up with my favorites and I knew I can't go wrong with the flavors. Fun and cool toppings to add.

Glazed Milky Bun + Salted Caramel + Cookie Butter + a sprinkle of lucky charms= sweet warm buttery orgasmic milky bang goodness!!!!

Then you feel like going for a walk after that, but totally worth getting fat for! :)

I'm coming back to try the churro and Vietnamese coffee ice cream!!!< /review>

<Text>The Hype: The glazed milky bun, which is a donut.

The Yum: Their ice cream quality is top notch. I really love their creative flavors such as the cookie monster, churro ice cream, viet coffee, etc.

Jasmine Milk Tea ice cream: I do recommend it. It's not too sugary and it's not super rich.

The Line: It wasn't that long and it gave me time to read some yelp reviews to see what to get.

Tips:
If you still want the milky bun with ice cream then get it without the glaze. The glaze will stick to the paper wrap and the sugar will take over the ice cream flavor. My head hurts from the sugar high I got from it.

If you want the milky bun sealed or filled, they will warm up the bun so your ice cream will melt faster.

Best to get just the ice cream... unless this is your first time here then it doesn't hurt to get the bun so you can cross it off your foodie-list.<//Text><Pictures>None<//Pictures><Resp>None< /Resp><GmapID>0x80dd27390c3fe7ab:0x98c5e2648edf90f4<//GmapID></record>

< Review>
Went for the very first time yesterday and O-M-G, they're doing ice cream right! I got a nostalgia flavor of pineapple & cherry (growing up with Big Stix) and my partner got a mint monster with fruity pebbles in a milky bun. I honestly thought the idea of ice cream in a doughnut sounded way too sweet for my taste but it was just the right amount of creamy and the crunchiness from the Fruity Pebbles was the perfect touch! < text>
Came here one Sunday afternoon and was surprised to find a line outside of the shop! I debated not waiting but figured why not? In the 45 min line, my sister, parents and myself all decided that we wanted to try the glazed milky bun ($5) with different ice creams.

For $5, you can get the bun (glazed or non-glazed) with ice cream in the middle and one topping. They had a pretty good variety of flavors and toppings to choose from.

I personally had the churro bun with oreo bits but also sampled the below:

-cookie monster
-strawberry
-cookie butter

All of them were really really delicious. It was hard to distinguish the exact quality of the ice cream because it was overwhelmed by the taste of the glazed donut. That being said - the overall combo was sweet, messy goodness and I did enjoy the churro flavor.

Not sure if I would wait in that line again but I'd definitely come back again if I'm in the area.<//text>

<Review>DONUT + ICE CREAM = $$$$

Throughout the years I'm constantly seeing new and hyped up creations from the ramen burger to the cronut. I mean the idea is great and all but I think these things are seriously overhyped and unfortunately the same goes for the Milky Buns at Afters.

When I heard the line for Afters averages 45mins -1 hr long I knew it probably wouldn't be worth the wait. I had friends tell me about this place and show me pictures of the famous Milky Buns so being a foodie i knew i had to try it for myself. Luckily, this past weekend Jen H. and I dropped by after the Color Run around 2pm on Saturday and to our surprise there was no line! We waited about 5 minutes! So if you want to try this place I highly suggest coming here in the afternoon to avoid the crazy teens that gather here at night.

In terms of the dessert itself, I thought the handmade ice cream was delicious. I sampled a couple flavors and fell in love with the Acai blueberry because I love fruity flavors. The Milky Bun comes with one topping for around $5. I got fruity pebbles and it gave the Milky Bun ice cream sandwich a nice crunch and paired very well with the ice cream. As a whole, the Milky Bun tasted just like a donut ice cream sandwich. Imagine if you were to add really good ice cream inside a glazed donut then you would get the Milky Bun. There really isn't much to it then that so hype or no hype if you must try come during the off hours because the wait is ridiculous if you come at night.< /Review><Pictures>None<//Pictures><resp>None</resp>< gmapID>

<Pics>None<//Pics><name>Walter Macalma</name><Resp>None</Resp><text>Disclaimer: In depth review lies ahead.

Long has the tradition been the dessert come post meal, but years ago I met a man who was so in love with his dessert that he ate it first, knowing that if he were to get full and unable to finish his meal the 1 thing he wasn't going to miss was dessert so he would also often skip appetizers. It's on that premise that I think the name After's plays on, because I think the same effect would occur if they called it "And then".

Todays social media has changed the game in how we market. Beyond the website it's FB, IG, Vine and Twitter that are making the biggest strides. I actually think that the website is a little light on the features.  it's nice and all, fancy and bright, but not really intuitive or informative, just heavy on the pictures, links and promotion. I found out about Afters through IG and not Yelp or friends, that's a first since I'm obviously pretty active yelp hunter.

The signage is really just remnants and a little sketchy compared to the work they put in online. The seating is not tended to or cleaned as often as they are pushing out product. The parking lot is littered, literally with wrappers, melted ice cream and just junk. It looks like a parking lot after a sporting event. They need WAY more trash cans, more tables would be nice too, but not necessary. I don't mind coming here and eating here, but this isn't Starbucks where you set up your laptop and do HW, it's busy, it's packed and hanging around is wasting space when you see how many people want this stuff. DÃ©cor inside is stark and basic, 2 toned paint and I get the current Gucci mane reference, but it's kind of permanent for someone who has an expiration date on relevance. Maybe put that 1 in chalk or on a monitor versus paint. Wait can be up to an hour.

I LOVE the monthly changing menu. Check the website with progressive flavors like Milk & Cereal (though I never added sugar to my cereal I know some kids growing up who did, I think it's a regional or cultural thing). Smooth, not too rich, unique. Vietnamese Coffee is  bold up front, but doesn't linger and isn't highly caffeinated like the coffee itself.  Churro is a little gritty and is excellent with caramel as I try to go for the dulce de leche end note. Jasmin Milk tea is a good replica of the typical milk tea you get from boba spots, but since it's ice cream it's quite a bit thicker. Almond cookie is liquid macaroons and great when you get it alone, no toppings. Cookie Monster to me was a bit of a bust. Their rocky road could use more nuts and marshmallows.

It would be nice to have fresh pressed waffle cones and standard made upon ordering. Many of their flavors are so rich you almost need something to mellow them out or go no toppings and in a cup, not cone. NOW onto the star of the show the Milky Bun which is basically a donut, sliced in half, stuffed with your choice of ice cream and toppings and resealed. There are large variences in workmanship as I've had picturesque and then abominations made. The glazed even when eaten right away is messy so go plain and no toppings is my preference. You really can't eat just one, so why wait in line all that time to realize it. Buy 2 and don't be disappointed.

I like the concept, and the ice cream, marketing is on point, but using an old Mexican food shop in a shopping center that probably couldn't handle you popularity or need for immediate expansion lacked some foresight. Oh the curse of innovation. It's a great place to come eat after you get  G Burger across the parking lot. Warning: I've seen 2 people be distracted and hit pedestrians here. Parking lot is dangerous so don't' be distracted walking or driving. My guess is you'll see flavored buns here soon. May your ice cream be high and fat and your buns always be milky.< /text><Rate>4</Rate>< gmapID>

<Rate>4</Rate><Text>I may never have found out about this place if not for my good friends at Bobalife, (if you love all things boba/cutesy/Asian, I suggest you look them up), and when you have an endorsement by 2 people who clearly know their sweets, you bet I'm going to drive an hour to try these ice cream-stuffed milky buns.

First off, I have to strongly urge you to show up at least 15 minutes before they open, as the lines get hella long, and they stay that way indefinitely. Secondly, these guys have some really unique & delicious ice cream flavors on the menu, so you'll want to bring a friend or two to split a couple of milky buns/ice cream cups. Lastly, bring your appetite; ice cream wedged in between a big glazed donut = sweets overload.

All that being said, who doesn't love the idea of an ice cream sandwich made with a gorgeous piece of sweetly fried Heaven that is the Milky Bun? It's fairly simply: You decide whether or not you want the ice cream in a milky bun, (and why wouldn't you?). You choose your flavor. You add a topping. You pay. You go outside, and try to find a secluded area where you can stuff your face, as the delicious, messy ice cream runs down your fingers. Repeat, if necessary.
With the smorgasbord of flavors like, Churro, Cookie Butter, Vietnamese Coffee, & Jasmine Milk Tea, and toppings like Cap'n Crunch cereal & chocolate chips, you'll want to use the time spent in line to plan your order to waste as little time as possible. Once you're there, you're a bit pressured to move quickly.
Want my advice? Try the most popular combinations of a glazed milky bun with cookie butter, topped with Cap'n Crunch cereal. Or if you're feeling like some java, go for the Vietnamese Coffee topped with some chocolate chips.

Just don't do what I did, show up alone, and then decide to get two stuffed milky buns and scarf them down at the same time. I'm still recovering from the food coma.<//Text><pictures>None<//pictures>< resp>

<Name>Rodney S<//Name><Date>1415650200023< /Date><rate>4</rate>< Text>
"So I sing you to sleep, after the lovin." - "After the Lovin", Englebert Humperdinck

I first heard of AFTERS Handcrafted Ice Cream during a segment on the KTLA Morning News, featuring their trademark "Milky Buns" & their variety of unique flavors.  I knew right away that I had to move my hot ass on over there someday, and with plans on having dinner at the nearby Shin Sen Gumi Robata & Yakitori, it was the perfect opportunity to come in & and see what all the fuss was about.

AFTERS is located on Brookhurst & Talbert, in Fountain Valley.  If you're looking for a big AFTERS sign, you're SOL.  Just look for ICE CREAM on the left of the plaza, and you've found it.

The friendly employees will kindly let you sample whatever you like.

Around 6pm on a Monday night, with only a few people in line.  Perfect timing by yours truly.

Donuts aren't really my thing, so I already had in mind to have strictly ice cream.  I refer to donuts as "heart attack food".  One of the most unhealthiest things to eat.  I already imagine a "Milky Bun" to be way too sweet for me, so I can share my own unbiased opinion on the "coup de grace" of any ice cream parlor - the ice cream!

Of all that I tried, my favorites were the churro, milk & cereal, jasmine milk tea & Vietnamese coffee.

Each had the distinct flavor of their namesakes.  I loved the crunch of the Frosted Flakes in the milk & cereal.  All had great creamy texture that good ice cream should have.

Service was good.  The employees didn't hesitate to let me sample whatever I'd like.  There are a few outdoor tables to sit & enjoy your ice cream.  Parking is in private lot.

AFTERS Handcrafted Ice Cream makes high quality ice cream in a unique assortment of fun flavors.  I don't think I'd go out of my way to return for more ice cream, but if I'm in the area, I definitely see myself diving in for another scoop or 4 ;p

Highly recommend!
NOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOM< /Text>
